href="https://www.klm.com/">klm.com</a></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<p><b>KLM Royal Dutch Airlines</b>, legally <i><a href="/wiki/Koninklijk" title="Koninklijk">Koninklijke</a> Luchtvaart Maatschappij <a href="/wiki/Naamloze_vennootschap" title="Naamloze vennootschap">N.V.</a></i> (literal translation: Royal Aviation Company, Inc.),<sup id="cite_ref-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-6">&#91;6&#93;</a></sup> is the <a href="/wiki/Flag_carrier" title="Flag carrier">flag carrier</a> airline of the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> KLM is headquartered in <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a>, with its hub at nearby <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>. It is part of the <a href="/wiki/Air_France%E2%80%93KLM" title="Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM">Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM</a> group and a member of the <a href="/wiki/SkyTeam" title="SkyTeam">SkyTeam</a> airline alliance. Founded in 1919, KLM is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_airlines_by_foundation_date" title="List of airlines by foundation date">oldest airline in the world</a> still operating under its original name and had 35,488 employees and a fleet of 119 (excluding subsidiaries) as of 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>.<sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> KLM operates scheduled passenger and cargo services to <a href="/wiki/List_of_KLM_destinations" title="List of KLM destinations">145 destinations</a>.\n</p>\n<style class="tocnumber">9</span> <span class="toctext">See also</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-45"><a href="#References"><span class="tocnumber">10</span> <span class="toctext">References</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-46"><a href="#Bibliography"><span class="tocnumber">11</span> <span class="toctext">Bibliography</span></a></li>\n<li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-47"><a href="#External_links"><span class="tocnumber">12</span> <span class="toctext">External links</span></a></li>\n</ul>\n</div>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_years">Early years</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early years">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Klm-poster-1919.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bf/Klm-poster-1919.jpg/220px-Klm-poster-1919.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="299" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/b/bf/Klm-poster-1919.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="260" data-file-height="353" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Klm-poster-1919.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM poster featuring the airline\'s first commercial slogan. It is likely dated around the late 1920s, after it started service to Batavia.<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1919, a young aviator lieutenant named <a href="/wiki/Albert_Plesman" title="Albert Plesman">Albert Plesman</a> sponsored the ELTA aviation exhibition in <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam" title="Amsterdam">Amsterdam</a>. The exhibition was a great success; after it closed, several Dutch commercial interests intended to establish a Dutch airline, which Plesman was nominated to head.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In September 1919, <a href="/wiki/Wilhelmina_of_the_Netherlands" title="Wilhelmina of the Netherlands">Queen Wilhelmina</a> awarded the yet-to-be-founded KLM its "Royal" ("<i><a href="/wiki/Koninklijk" title="Koninklijk">Koninklijke</a></i>") predicate.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 7 October 1919, eight Dutch businessmen, including <a href="/wiki/Frits_Fentener_van_Vlissingen_(1882)" title="Frits Fentener van Vlissingen (1882)">Frits Fentener van Vlissingen</a>, founded KLM as one of the first commercial airline companies. Plesman became its first administrator and director.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The first KLM flight took place on 17 May 1920. KLM\'s first pilot, Jerry Shaw, flew from <a href="/wiki/Croydon_Airport" title="Croydon Airport">Croydon Airport</a>, London, to Amsterdam.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The flight was flown using a leased <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_Transport_and_Travel" title="Aircraft Transport and Travel">Aircraft Transport and Travel</a> <a href="/wiki/Airco_DH.16" title="Airco DH.16">De Haviland DH-16</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> registration G-EALU, which was carrying two British journalists and some newspapers. In 1920, KLM carried 440 passengers and 22 tons of freight. In April 1921, after a winter hiatus, KLM resumed its services using its pilots, and <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.II" title="Fokker F.II">Fokker F.II</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.III" title="Fokker F.III">Fokker F.III</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1921, KLM started scheduled services.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg/220px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg/330px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg/440px-COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="521" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Groepsportret_voorafgaand_aan_het_vertrek_van_directeur_Rendorp_van_de_KNILM_per_Fokker_F-XII_van_de_KLM_naar_Nederland_TMnr_60027465.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM Fokker F-XVIII departing from the Dutch East Indies, 1932</div></div></div>\n<p>KLM\'s first intercontinental flight took off on 1 October 1924.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The final destination was <a href="/wiki/Halim_Perdanakusuma_International_Airport" title="Halim Perdanakusuma International Airport">Jakarta</a> (then called \'<a href="/wiki/Batavia,_Dutch_East_Indies" title="Batavia, Dutch East Indies">Batavia</a>\'), <a href="/wiki/Java" title="Java">Java</a>, in the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_Indies" title="Dutch East Indies">Dutch East Indies</a>; the flight used a <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.VII" title="Fokker F.VII">Fokker F.VII</a><sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> with registration H-NACC and was piloted by Van der Hoop.<sup id="cite_ref-Aviacrash_H-NACC_12-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Aviacrash_H-NACC-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup> In September 1929, regular scheduled services between Amsterdam and Batavia commenced. Until the outbreak of the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a> in 1939, this was the world\'s longest-distance scheduled service by airplane.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> By 1926, it was offering flights to Amsterdam, Rotterdam, Brussels, Paris, London, Bremen, Copenhagen, and Malm\xc3\xb6, using primarily Fokker F.II and Fokker F.III aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-Heijn_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Heijn-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_groep_Europeanen_staat_op_het_vliegveld_Rambang_voor_het_vliegtuig_de_Uiver_dat_is_aangekomen_op_Lombok_na_afloop_van_de_London-Melbourne-race_in_1934_TMnr_10010712.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_groep_Europeanen_staat_op_het_vliegveld_Rambang_voor_het_vliegtuig_de_Uiver_dat_is_aangekomen_op_Lombok_na_afloop_van_de_London-Melbourne-race_in_1934_TMnr_10010712.jpg/220px-thumbnail.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_groep_Europeanen_staat_op_het_vliegveld_Rambang_voor_het_vliegtuig_de_Uiver_dat_is_aangekomen_op_Lombok_na_afloop_van_de_London-Melbourne-race_in_1934_TMnr_10010712.jpg/330px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/09/COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_groep_Europeanen_staat_op_het_vliegveld_Rambang_voor_het_vliegtuig_de_Uiver_dat_is_aangekomen_op_Lombok_na_afloop_van_de_London-Melbourne-race_in_1934_TMnr_10010712.jpg/440px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="468" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:COLLECTIE_TROPENMUSEUM_Een_groep_Europeanen_staat_op_het_vliegveld_Rambang_voor_het_vliegtuig_de_Uiver_dat_is_aangekomen_op_Lombok_na_afloop_van_de_London-Melbourne-race_in_1934_TMnr_10010712.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-2" title="Douglas DC-2">Douglas DC-2</a> aircraft <i>Uiver</i> in transit at Rambang airfield on the east coast of <a href="/wiki/Lombok" title="Lombok">Lombok</a> island following the aircraft being placed second in the <a href="/wiki/MacRobertson_Air_Race" title="MacRobertson Air Race">MacRobertson Air Race</a> from <a href="/wiki/RAF_Mildenhall" title="RAF Mildenhall">RAF Mildenhall</a>, England, to Melbourne in 1934.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1930, KLM carried 15,143 passengers. The <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-2" title="Douglas DC-2">Douglas DC-2</a> was introduced on the Batavia service in 1934. The first experimental transatlantic KLM flight was between Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a> in December 1934 using the <a href="/wiki/Fokker_F.XVIII" title="Fokker F.XVIII">Fokker F.XVIII</a> "Snip".<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The first of the airline\'s <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> aircraft were delivered in 1936; these replaced the DC-2s on the service via Batavia to <a href="/wiki/Sydney_Airport" title="Sydney Airport">Sydney</a>. KLM was the first airline to serve <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester\'s new Ringway airport</a>, starting June 1938. KLM was the only civilian airline to receive the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-5" title="Douglas DC-5">Douglas DC-5</a>; the airline used two of them in the West Indies and sold two to the East Indies government, and is thus the only airline to have operated all Douglas \'DC\' models other than the DC-1.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb  tleft">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:200px;font-size:88%">\n<table class="wikitable" style="display:table;background: #fefefe;width:100%;margin-top:0;text-align:center">\n<caption style="display:table-caption">\nRevenue Passenger-Kilometers, scheduled flights only, in millions\n</caption>\n<tbody><tr>\n<th>Year</th>\n<th>Traffic\n</th></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1947\n</td>\n<td>0,454\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1950\n</td>\n<td>0,766\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1955\n</td>\n<td>1,485\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1960\n</td>\n<td>2,660\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1965\n</td>\n<td>3,342\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1971\n</td>\n<td>6,330\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1975\n</td>\n<td>10,077\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1980\n</td>\n<td>14,058\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1985\n</td>\n<td>18,039\n</td></tr>\n<tr>\n<td>1995\n</td>\n<td>44,458\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<div style="font-size:8pt;text-align:left">Source: ICAO Digest of Statistics for 1947\xe2\x80\x9355, IATA World Air Transport Statistics 1960\xe2\x80\x931995</div>\n</div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Second_World_War">Second World War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Second World War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Further information: <a href="/wiki/1942_KNILM_Douglas_DC-3_shootdown" title="1942 KNILM Douglas DC-3 shootdown">1942 KNILM Douglas DC-3 shootdown</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg/220px-Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="136" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg/330px-Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5d/Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg/440px-Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1078" data-file-height="667" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_C-47A_PH-TBP_KLM_ed_Ringway_20.05.47_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">Douglas DC-3</a> at <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Airport" title="Manchester Airport">Manchester Airport</a> in 1947</div></div></div>\n<p>When Germany invaded the Netherlands on 10 May 1940, several KLM aircraft\xe2\x80\x94mostly DC-3s and a few DC-2s\xe2\x80\x94were en route to or from the Far East, or were operating services in Europe. Five <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">DC-3s</a> and one <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-2" title="Douglas DC-2">DC-2</a> were taken to Britain. During the war, these aircraft and crew members flew scheduled passenger flights between Bristol and Lisbon under <a href="/wiki/British_Overseas_Airways_Corporation" title="British Overseas Airways Corporation">BOAC</a> registration.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>The Douglas DC-3 PH-ALI "Ibis", then registered as G-AGBB, was attacked by the <a href="/wiki/Luftwaffe" title="Luftwaffe">Luftwaffe</a> on 15 November 1942, 19 April 1943, and finally on 1 June 1943 as <a href="/wiki/BOAC_Flight_777" title="BOAC Flight 777">BOAC Flight 777</a>, killing all passengers and crew. Some KLM aircraft and their crews ended up in the Australia-Dutch East Indies region, where they helped transport refugees from Japanese aggression in that area.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Although operations paused in Europe, KLM continued to fly and expand in the Caribbean.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Also during the Second World War a KLM <a href="/wiki/1942_KNILM_Douglas_DC-3_shootdown" title="1942 KNILM Douglas DC-3 shootdown">flight</a> carrying eight passengers, four crew and a 2020 value of $15 million in diamonds was shot down by Japanese fighters returning from the <a href="/wiki/Attack_on_Broome" title="Attack on Broome">Attack on Broome</a> approximately 1,000 miles north of <a href="/wiki/Perth" title="Perth">Perth</a> in <a href="/wiki/Western_Australia" title="Western Australia">Western Australia</a>. The pilot managed to dive to evade the fighters and crash land on the beach but three passengers and one crewman were killed. After six days and suffering other attacks by strafing Japanese pilots they were rescued. The diamonds may have been heisted by a survivor or civilian happening upon the wreck soon after.\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Post-World_War_II">Post-World War II</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Post-World War II">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>After the end of the Second World War in August 1945, KLM immediately started to rebuild its network. Since the Dutch East Indies were in a <a href="/wiki/Indonesian_National_Revolution" title="Indonesian National Revolution">state of revolt</a>, Plesman\'s priority was to re-establish KLM\'s route to Batavia. This service was reinstated by the end of 1945.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Domestic and European flights resumed in September 1945, initially with a fleet of Douglas <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-3" title="Douglas DC-3">DC-3s</a> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-4" title="Douglas DC-4">Douglas DC-4s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 21 May 1946, KLM was the first continental European airline to start scheduled transatlantic flights between Amsterdam and <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">New York City</a> using Douglas DC-4 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> By 1948, KLM had reconstructed its network and services to Africa, North and South America, and the <a href="/wiki/Caribbean" title="Caribbean">Caribbean</a> resumed.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg/220px-Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg/330px-Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/88/Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg/440px-Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="655" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L-749A_PH-TDK_KLM_RWY_07.07.53_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Constellation" title="Lockheed Constellation">Lockheed L-749A Constellation</a> of KLM in 1953</div></div></div>\n<p>Long-range, pressurized <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Constellation" title="Lockheed Constellation">Lockheed Constellations</a><sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-6" title="Douglas DC-6">Douglas DC-6s</a><sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> joined KLM\'s fleet in the late 1940s; the <a href="/wiki/Convair_240" class="mw-redirect" title="Convair 240">Convair 240</a> short-range pressurized twin-engined airliner began European flights for the company in late 1948.<sup id="cite_ref-(Airline)1953_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-(Airline)1953-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>During the immediate post-war period, the Dutch government expressed interest in gaining a majority stake in KLM, thus partially nationalizing it. Plesman wanted KLM to remain a private company under private control; he allowed the Dutch government to acquire a minority stake in the airline.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1950, KLM carried 356,069 passengers. The expansion of the network continued in the 1950s with the addition of several destinations in western North America.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> KLM\'s fleet expanded with the addition of new versions of the Lockheed Constellation and <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-188_Electra" title="Lockheed L-188 Electra">Lockheed Electra</a>, of which KLM was the first European airline to fly.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg/220px-Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="132" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg/330px-Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/54/Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg/440px-Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1025" data-file-height="616" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Vickers_Viscount_803_PH-VIF_KLM_RWY_08.64_edited-4.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> 803</div></div></div>\n<p>On 31 December 1953, the founder and president of KLM, Albert Plesman, died at the age of 64.<sup id="cite_ref-FI_founder_1959_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FI_founder_1959-1">&#91;1&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-FI_founder_1971_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FI_founder_1971-2">&#91;2&#93;</a></sup> He was succeeded as president by <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fons_Aler&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fons Aler (page does not exist)">Fons Aler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> After Plesman\'s death, the company and other airlines entered a difficult economic period. The conversion to jet aircraft placed a further financial burden on KLM. The Netherlands government increased its ownership of the company to two-thirds, thus partly nationalizing it. The board of directors remained under the control of private shareholders.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-7" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 25 July 1957, the airline introduced its flight simulator for the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-7" title="Douglas DC-7">Douglas DC-7</a>C \xe2\x80\x93 the last KLM aircraft with piston engines \xe2\x80\x93 which opened the transpolar route from Amsterdam via <a href="/wiki/Anchorage" class="mw-redirect" title="Anchorage">Anchorage</a> to <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a> on 1 November 1958.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> Each crew flying the transpolar route over the Arctic was equipped with a winter survival kit, including a 7.62&#160;mm selective-fire <a href="/wiki/AR-10" class="mw-redirect" title="AR-10">AR-10</a> carbine for use against polar bears, in the event the plane was forced down onto the polar ice.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Jet_age">Jet age</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Jet age">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The four-engine turboprop <a href="/wiki/Vickers_Viscount" title="Vickers Viscount">Vickers Viscount</a> 800 was introduced on European routes in 1957.<sup id="cite_ref-Airline_Timetable_Images_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airline_Timetable_Images-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in September 1959, KLM introduced the four-engine turboprop <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-188_Electra" title="Lockheed L-188 Electra">Lockheed L-188 Electra</a> onto some of its European and Middle Eastern routes. In March 1960, the airline introduced the first <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8" title="Douglas DC-8">Douglas DC-8</a> jet into its fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1961, KLM reported its first year of losses.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1961, the airline\'s president Fons Aler was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Ernst_van_der_Beugel" title="Ernst van der Beugel">Ernst van der Beugel</a>. This change of leadership, however, did not lead to a reversal of KLM\'s financial difficulties.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Van der Beugel resigned as president in 1963 due to health reasons.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> Horatius Albarda was appointed to succeed Ernst van der Beugel as president of KLM in 1963.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup> Alberda initiated a reorganization of the company, which led to the reduction of staff and air services.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1965, Alberda died in an air crash and was succeeded as president by Dr. Gerrit van der Wal.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Van der Wal forged an agreement with the Dutch government that KLM would be once again run as a private company. By 1966, the stake of the Dutch government in KLM was reduced to a minority stake of 49.5%.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In 1966, KLM introduced the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-9" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas DC-9">Douglas DC-9</a> on European and Middle East routes.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg/220px-Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="108" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg/330px-Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg/440px-Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="752" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_188_Electra_PH-LLD_KLM_07.65.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_L-188_Electra" title="Lockheed L-188 Electra">Lockheed L-188 Electra</a> turboprop airliner in 1965</div></div></div>\n<p>The new terminal buildings at <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a> opened in April 1967, and in 1968 the stretched <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8-63" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas DC-8-63">Douglas DC-8-63</a> ("Super DC-8") entered service.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> With 244 seats, it was the largest airliner at the time. KLM was the first airline to put the higher-gross-weight <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-200</a>B, powered by <a href="/wiki/Pratt_%26_Whitney_JT9D" title="Pratt &amp; Whitney JT9D">Pratt &amp; Whitney JT9D</a> engines, into service in February 1971;<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> this began the airline\'s use of <a href="/wiki/Widebody" class="mw-redirect" title="Widebody">widebody</a> jets.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In March 1971, KLM opened its current headquarters in <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1972, it purchased the first of several <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a> aircraft\xe2\x80\x94McDonnell Douglas\'s response to <a href="/wiki/Boeing" title="Boeing">Boeing</a>\'s 747.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-206B,_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg/220px-Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="106" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg/330px-Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bc/Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg/440px-Boeing_747-206B%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg 2x" data-file-width="723" data-file-height="348" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Boeing_747-206B,_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN0006613.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM Boeing 747-206B in 1971.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 1973, Sergio Orlandini was appointed to succeed Gerrit van der Wal as president of KLM.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup> At the time, KLM, as well as other airlines, had to deal with overcapacity. Orlandini proposed to convert KLM 747s to "combis" that could carry a combination of passengers and freight in a mixed configuration on the main deck of the aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> In November 1975, the first of these seven <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200">Boeing 747-200</a>B <a href="/wiki/Combi_aircraft" title="Combi aircraft">Combi aircraft</a> were added to the KLM fleet.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The airline previously operated DC-8 passenger and freight combi aircraft as well and currently operates <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> combi aircraft.\n</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/1973_oil_crisis" title="1973 oil crisis">1973 oil crisis</a>, which caused difficult economic conditions, led KLM to seek government assistance in arranging debt refinancing. The airline issued additional shares of stock to the government in return for its money. In the late 1970s, the government\'s stake had again increased to a majority of 78%, effectively re-nationalizing it.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The company management remained under the control of private stakeholders.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1980s_and_1990s">1980s and 1990s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1980s and 1990s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63,_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg/220px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="151" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg/330px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg/440px-McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63%2C_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="701" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McDonnell_Douglas_DC-8-63,_KLM_-_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_AN1108402.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM <a href="/wiki/Douglas_DC-8-63" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas DC-8-63">Douglas DC-8-63</a> at <a href="/wiki/London_Heathrow_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="London Heathrow Airport">London Heathrow Airport</a> in 1982.  The DC-8 was the mainstay of the KLM narrowbody jet fleet.</div></div></div>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r978413945/mw-parser-output/.tmulti">.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle{float:none!important;max-width:100%!important;box-sizing:border-box;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .tsingle .thumbcaption{text-align:left}.mw-parser-output .tmulti .trow>.thumbcaption{text-align:center}}</style><div class="thumb tmulti tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:224px;max-width:224px"><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_Spijkers.jpg/330px-Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_Spijkers.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3a/Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_Spijkers.jpg/440px-Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_Spijkers.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1023" data-file-height="711" /></a></div><div class="thumbcaption">A <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-10" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-10">McDonnell Douglas DC-10</a> operated by <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a> (tail number N237NW) in a hybrid Northwest-KLM livery (1999). This photo shows the starboard (above) and port side of the aircraft (below)</div></div></div><div class="trow"><div class="tsingle" style="width:222px;max-width:222px"><div class="thumbimage"><a href="/wiki/File:Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg/220px-Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="134" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg/330px-Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c9/Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg/440px-Northwest_Airlines-KLM_DC-10_hybrid_livery_KvW.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="486" /></a></div></div></div></div></div>\n<p>In 1980, KLM carried 9,715,069 passengers. In 1983, it reached an agreement with Boeing to convert ten of its Boeing 747-200 aircraft (Three 747-200Bs and Seven 747-200Ms) into Boeing 747-300s with the stretched-upper-deck modification. The work started in 1984 at the Boeing factory in <a href="/wiki/Everett,_Washington" title="Everett, Washington">Everett, Washington</a>, and finished in 1986. The converted aircraft were called Boeing 747-200SUD or 747-300, which the airline operated in addition to three newly built Boeing 747-300s manufactured from the ground up. In 1983, KLM took delivery of the first of ten <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A310" title="Airbus A310">Airbus A310</a> passenger jets.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Sergio Orlandini retired in 1987 and was succeeded as president of KLM by Jan de Soet.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup> In 1986, the Dutch government\'s shareholding in KLM was reduced to 54.8 percent.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> It was expected that this share would be further reduced during the decade.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400</a> was introduced into KLM\'s fleet in June 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With the liberalization of the European market, KLM started developing its hub at Amsterdam Airport Schiphol by feeding its network with traffic from affiliated airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> As part of its development of a worldwide network, KLM acquired a 20% stake in <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Airlines" title="Northwest Airlines">Northwest Airlines</a> in July 1989.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1990, KLM carried 16,000,000 passengers. KLM president Jan de Soet retired at the end of 1990 and was succeeded in 1991 by Pieter Bouw.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup> In December 1991, KLM was the first European airline to introduce a frequent flyer loyalty program, which was called <i>Flying Dutchman</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Joint_venture">Joint venture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Joint venture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>In January 1993, the United States Department of Transportation granted KLM and Northwest Airlines anti-trust immunity, which allowed them to intensify their partnership.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> As of September 1993, the airlines operated their flights between the United States and Europe as part of a joint venture.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In March 1994, KLM and Northwest Airlines introduced World Business Class on intercontinental routes.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> KLM\'s stake in Northwest Airlines was increased to 25% in 1994.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistoryFU_10-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistoryFU-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM introduced the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_767" title="Boeing 767">Boeing 767-300ER</a> in July 1995.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In January 1996, KLM acquired a 26% share in <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a>, the flag-carrier airline of Kenya.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> In 1997, Pieter Bouw resigned as president of KLM and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/L._M._van_Wijk" title="L. M. van Wijk">Leo van Wijk</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> In August 1998, KLM repurchased all regular shares from the Dutch government to make KLM a private company.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> On 1 November 1999, KLM founded AirCares, a communication and fundraising platform supporting worthy causes and focusing on underprivileged children.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM renewed its intercontinental fleets by replacing the Boeing 767s, Boeing 747-300s, and eventually, the <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_MD-11" title="McDonnell Douglas MD-11">McDonnell Douglas MD-11s</a> with <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777" title="Boeing 777">Boeing 777-200ERs</a> and <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A330" title="Airbus A330">Airbus A330-200s</a>. Some 747s were withdrawn from service first. The MD-11s remained in service until October 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup> The first Boeing 777 was received on 25 October 2003, while the first Airbus A330-200 was introduced on 25 August 2005.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHistory_11-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHistory-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span id="Air_France.E2.80.93KLM_merger"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Air_France\xe2\x80\x93KLM_merger">Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM merger</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM merger">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On 30 September 2003, <a href="/wiki/Air_France" title="Air France">Air France</a> and KLM agreed to a merger plan in which Air France and KLM would become subsidiaries of a holding company called <a href="/wiki/Air_France%E2%80%93KLM" title="Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM">Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM</a>. Both airlines would retain their own brands; both <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Charles de Gaulle Airport</a> and <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a> would become key hubs.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup> In February 2004, the <a href="/wiki/European_Commission" title="European Commission">European Commission</a> and <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_Justice" title="United States Department of Justice">United States Department of Justice</a> approved the proposed merger of the airlines.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup> In April 2004, an exchange offer in which KLM shareholders exchanged their KLM shares for Air France shares took place.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> Since 5 May 2004, Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM has been listed on the <a href="/wiki/Euronext" title="Euronext">Euronext</a> exchanges in Paris, Amsterdam and New York.<sup id="cite_ref-referencedoc0405_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referencedoc0405-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> In September 2004, the merger was completed by creation of the Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM holding company.<sup id="cite_ref-referencedoc0405_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-referencedoc0405-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> The merger resulted in the world\'s largest airline group and should have led to an estimated annual cost-saving of between \xe2\x82\xac400 million and \xe2\x82\xac500 million.<sup id="cite_ref-afklmergerdeal_38-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-afklmergerdeal-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>It did not appear that KLM\'s longstanding joint venture with Northwest Airlines\xe2\x80\x94which merged with <a href="/wiki/Delta_Air_Lines" title="Delta Air Lines">Delta Air Lines</a> in 2008\xe2\x80\x94was affected by the merger with Air France. KLM and Northwest joined the SkyTeam alliance in September 2004. Also in 2004, senior management came under fire for providing itself with controversial bonuses after the merger with Air France, while 4,500 jobs were lost at KLM. After external pressure, management gave up on these bonuses.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In March 2007, KLM started to use the <a href="/wiki/Amadeus_CRS" title="Amadeus CRS">Amadeus</a> reservation system, along with partner Kenya Airways. After 10 years as president of the airline, Leo van Wijk resigned from his position and was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Peter_Hartman" title="Peter Hartman">Peter Hartman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2010s">2010s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2010s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Beginning in September 2010, KLM integrated the passenger division of <a href="/wiki/Martinair" title="Martinair">Martinair</a> into KLM, transferring all personnel and routes. By November 2011, Martinair consisted of only the cargo and maintenance division.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup> In March 2011, KLM and <a href="/wiki/InselAir" class="mw-redirect" title="InselAir">InselAir</a> reached an agreement for mutual cooperation on InselAir destinations, thus expanding its passenger services. Beginning 27 March 2011, KLM passengers could fly to all InselAir destinations through InselAir\'s hubs in <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sint_Maarten" title="Sint Maarten">Sint Maarten</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> This cooperation was extended to a codeshare agreement in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> In early 2018, the cooperation with Inselair was terminated, including any interlining agreements, after Inselair found itself in financial difficulties which forced the airline to sell off part of its fleet and cancel some of its routes.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>\nOn 20 February 2013, KLM announced that Peter Hartman would resign as president and CEO of KLM on 1 July 2013. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Camiel_Eurlings" title="Camiel Eurlings">Camiel Eurlings</a>. Hartman remained employed by the company until he retired on 1 January 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup> On 15 October 2014, KLM announced that Eurlings, in joint consultation with the supervisory board, had decided to immediately resign as president and CEO. As of this date, he was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Pieter_Elbers" title="Pieter Elbers">Pieter Elbers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-elbersceo_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-elbersceo-3">&#91;3&#93;</a></sup> KLM received the award for "Best Airline Staff Service" in Europe at the World Airline Awards 2013. This award represents the rating for an airline\'s performance across both airport staff and cabin staff combined.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup> It is the second consecutive year that KLM won this award; in 2012 it was awarded with this title as well.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup> On 19 June 2012, KLM made the first transatlantic flight fueled partly by sustainable biofuels to <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>. This was the longest distance any aircraft had flown on biofuels.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup> </p><div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:PH-BGU.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/PH-BGU.jpg/220px-PH-BGU.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/PH-BGU.jpg/330px-PH-BGU.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/5e/PH-BGU.jpg/440px-PH-BGU.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2442" data-file-height="1374" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:PH-BGU.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KLM <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737-700" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 737-700">Boeing 737-700</a> with a "100 year" livery taking off from <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Schiphol_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Schiphol Airport">Amsterdam Schiphol Airport</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>In 2019, KLM celebrated its centennial, as it was founded in 1919. Since it is the oldest airline still operating under its original name, it was the first airline to achieve this feat.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="2020s">2020s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2020s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>After cutting 5000 jobs in 2020, KLM said that it will cut 1000 jobs in 2021. It also said that the decisions of the government to have all the passengers and crew COVID-19 tested before flying will have an impact on its flights. <sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Corporate_affairs_and_identity">Corporate affairs and identity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Corporate affairs and identity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Business_trends">Business trends</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Business trends">edit</a><span href="#cite_note-KLM:_annual_Report_2018-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup>\n</td>\n<td align="center"><sup id="cite_ref-KLM:_annual_Report_2019_60-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLM:_annual_Report_2019-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup>\n</td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Management">Management</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Management">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>As of October 2015<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, KLM\'s corporate leader is its president and chief executive officer (CEO) Pieter Elbers, who replaced Camiel Eurlings suddenly on 15 October 2014. The president and CEO is part of the larger Executive Committee, which manages KLM and consists of the statutory managing directors and executive vice-presidents of KLM\'s business units that are represented in the Executive Committee.<sup id="cite_ref-klmmanagement_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klmmanagement-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup> The supervision and management of KLM are structured in accordance with the <i>two-tier model</i>; the Board of Managing Directors is supervised by a separate and independent <a href="/wiki/Supervisory_Board" class="mw-redirect" title="Supervisory Board">Supervisory Board</a>. The Supervisory Board also supervises the general performance of KLM.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup> The Board of Managing Directors is formed by the four Managing Directors, including the CEO. Nine Supervisory Directors compose the Supervisory Board.<sup id="cite_ref-klmmanagement_61-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klmmanagement-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Head_office">Head office</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Head office">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg/220px-KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg/330px-KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/53/KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg/440px-KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_hoofdkantoor_Amstelveen.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM head office in <a href="/wiki/Amstelveen" title="Amstelveen">Amstelveen</a></div></div></div>\n<p>KLM\'s head office is located in Amstelveen,<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> on a 6.5-hectare (16-acre) site near <a href="/wiki/Schiphol_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Schiphol Airport">Schiphol Airport</a>. The airline\'s current headquarters was built between 1968 and 1970.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup> Before the opening of the new headquarters, the airline\'s head office was on the property of Schiphol Airport in <a href="/wiki/Haarlemmermeer" title="Haarlemmermeer">Haarlemmermeer</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Subsidiaries">Subsidiaries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Subsidiaries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Companies in which KLM has a stake include:<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<table class="toccolours" border="1" cellpadding="3" DC-8">Douglas DC-8</a> and <a href="/wiki/McDonnell_Douglas_DC-9-30" class="mw-redirect" title="McDonnell Douglas DC-9-30">McDonnell Douglas DC-9-30</a> being operated by KLM flight crews on behalf of ALM.<sup id="cite_ref-Airline_Timetable_Images_21-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Airline_Timetable_Images-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="KLM_Asia">KLM Asia</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: KLM Asia">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_(4806800714).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg/220px-EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg/330px-EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg/440px-EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_%284806800714%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1280" data-file-height="948" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:EHAM18072010_PH-BFC_KLM_(4806800714).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>PH-BFC, notable for being involved in the <a href="/wiki/KLM_Flight_867" title="KLM Flight 867">Flight 867 incident</a>, was one of the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-400" title="Boeing 747-400">Boeing 747-400s</a> that served KLM from 1989 until its 14 March 2018 retirement. It became part of the KLM Asia fleet from 1995 until 2012, when it was repainted in the original KLM livery.</div></div></div>\n<p><b>KLM Asia</b> (<a href="/wiki/Traditional_Chinese_characters" title="Traditional Chinese characters">Chinese</a>&#58; <span lang="zh-Hant">\xe8\x8d\xb7\xe8\x98\xad\xe4\xba\x9e\xe6\xb4\xb2\xe8\x88\xaa\xe7\xa9\xba\xe5\x85\xac\xe5\x8f\xb8</span>; <a href="/wiki/Pinyin" title="Pinyin">pinyin</a>&#58; <i><span lang="zh-Latn-pinyin">H\xc3\xa9l\xc3\xa1n Y\xc3\xa0zh\xc5\x8du H\xc3\xa1ngk\xc5\x8dng G\xc5\x8dngs\xc4\xab</span></i>) is a wholly KLM-owned subsidiary registered in Taiwan. The airline was established in 1995 to operate flights to <a href="/wiki/Taipei" title="Taipei">Taipei</a> without compromising the traffic rights held by KLM for destinations in the People\'s Republic of China.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The livery of KLM Asia uses the same color scheme and livery of the original KLM but the only notable difference is that it lacks Dutch national symbols, such as the flag of the Netherlands and KLM\'s stylised <a href="/wiki/Monarchy_of_the_Netherlands" title="Monarchy of the Netherlands">Dutch Crown</a> logo. Instead, it features a special KLM Asia logo.\n</p><p>This division of the airline\'s fleet consists, as of March 2020, of seven <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-200ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-200ER">Boeing 777-200ER</a> and two <a href="/wiki/Boeing_777-300ER" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 777-300ER">Boeing 777-300ER</a> aircraft. KLM Asia initially operated the Amsterdam-<a href="/wiki/Suvarnabhumi_Airport" title="Suvarnabhumi Airport">Bangkok</a>-<a href="/wiki/Taiwan_Taoyuan_International_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Taiwan Taoyuan International Airport">Taipei</a> route with a B747-400 Combi or a B747-400 non-combi aircraft. Since March 2012, it has operated the revised Amsterdam-Taipei-<a href="/wiki/Ninoy_Aquino_International_Airport" title="Ninoy Aquino International Airport">Manila</a> route with Boeing 777-200ER/-300ER aircraft. Some aircraft are already painted in the revised KLM Asia livery of 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM Asia aircraft are also occasionally used to service other destinations in the wider KLM network.\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Branding">Branding</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Branding">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Dirk_Roosenburg" title="Dirk Roosenburg">Dirk Roosenburg</a> designed the KLM logo at its establishment in 1919; he intertwined the letter K, L, and M, and gave them wings and a <a href="/wiki/Crown_of_the_Netherlands" title="Crown of the Netherlands">crown</a>. The crown was depicted to denote KLM\'s royal status, which was granted at KLM\'s establishment.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup> The logo became known as the "vinklogo" in reference to the <a href="/wiki/Common_chaffinch" title="Common chaffinch">common chaffinch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> The KLM logo was largely redesigned in 1961 by <a href="/wiki/F.H.K._Henrion" class="mw-redirect" title="F.H.K. Henrion">F.H.K. Henrion</a>. The crown, redesigned using a line, four blue circles and a cross, was retained. In 1991, the logo was further revised by Chris Ludlow of Henrion, Ludlow &amp; Schmidt.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> In addition to its main logo, KLM displays its alliance status in its branding, including "Worldwide Reliability" with Northwest Airlines (1993\xe2\x80\x932002) and the SkyTeam alliance (2004\xe2\x80\x93present).<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<div style="clear:both;"></div>\n<div class="center"><div class="floatnone"><a href="/wiki/File:Evolution_klm.jpg" class="image" title="Evolution of the KLM logo"><img alt="Evolution of the KLM logo" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Evolution_klm.jpg/600px-Evolution_klm.jpg" decoding="async" width="600" height="394" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f7/Evolution_klm.jpg/900px-Evolution_klm.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/f/f7/Evolution_klm.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1000" data-file-height="657" /></a></div></div>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Livery_and_uniforms">Livery and uniforms</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Livery and uniforms">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Wing.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/KLM_Wing.jpg/220px-KLM_Wing.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="84" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/KLM_Wing.jpg/330px-KLM_Wing.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e9/KLM_Wing.jpg/440px-KLM_Wing.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2573" data-file-height="981" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Wing.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A current KLM pilot wing.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg/220px-Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8a/Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg/440px-Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="646" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Douglas_DC-6_PH-TPT_KLM_RWY_18.07.53_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>One of KLM\'s Douglas DC-6s in 1953.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg/220px-Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="153" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg/330px-Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1a/Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg/440px-Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="711" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Lockheed_L188C_PH-LLK_KLM_MAN_23.12.63_edited-2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A KLM Lockheed L-188 Electra in the airline\'s 1950s livery.</div></div></div>\n<p>KLM has utilized several major liveries since its founding, with numerous variations on each. Initially, many aircraft featured a bare-metal fuselage with a stripe above the windows bearing the phrase "The Flying Dutchman". The rudder was divided into three segments and painted to match the Dutch flag. Later aircraft types sometimes bore a white upper fuselage, and additional detail striping and titling. In the mid-1950s, the livery was changed to feature a split cheatline in two shades of blue on a white upper fuselage and angled blue stripes on the vertical stabilizer. The tail stripes were later enlarged and made horizontal, and the then-new crown logo was placed in a white circle. The final major variation of this livery saw the vertical stabilizer painted completely white with the crown logo in the center. All versions of this livery had small "KLM Royal Dutch Airlines" titles, first in red, and later in blue.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2020)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup>\n</p><p>Since 1971, the KLM livery has primarily featured a bright blue fuselage, with variations on the striping and details. Originally a wide, dark blue cheatline covered the windows and was separated from the light grey lower fuselage by a thin white stripe. The KLM logo was placed centrally on the white tail and the front of the fuselage. In December 2002, KLM introduced an updated livery in which the white strip was removed and the dark-blue cheatline was significantly narrowed. The bright blue colour was retained and now covers most of the fuselage. The KLM logo was placed more centrally on the fuselage while its position on the tail and the tail design remained the same.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> In 2014, KLM modified its livery with a swooping cheatline that wraps around the entire forward fuselage. The livery was first introduced on <a href="/wiki/Embraer_190" class="mw-redirect" title="Embraer 190">Embraer 190s</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In April 2010, KLM introduced new uniforms for its female cabin attendants, ground attendants and pilots at KLM and KLM Cityhopper. The new uniform was designed by Dutch couturier <a href="/wiki/Mart_Visser" title="Mart Visser">Mart Visser</a>. It retains the KLM blue colour that was introduced in 1971 and adds a touch of orange\xe2\x80\x94the national colour of the Netherlands.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing_slogans">Marketing slogans</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Marketing slogans">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>KLM has used several slogans for marketing throughout its operational history:\n</p>\n<ul><li>"<i>The businessman travels, sends, and receives by KLM</i>" (translated from Dutch)<sup id="cite_ref-klmreclames_97-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klmreclames-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> (1920s)</li>\n<li>"<i>The Flying Dutchman</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-klmreclames_97-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klmreclames-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>"<i>Bridging the World</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-klmreclames_97-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-klmreclames-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> (1994)</li>\n<li>"<i>The Reliable Airline</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-travelinsiderslogans_100-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelinsiderslogans-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>"<i>Journeys of Inspiration</i>"<sup id="cite_ref-travelinsiderslogans_100-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-travelinsiderslogans-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> (2009\xe2\x80\x93present)</li></ul>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Social_media">Social media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Social media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM has an extensive presence on <a href="/wiki/Social_media" title="Social media">social media</a> platforms and also runs a blog.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> Customers can make inquiries through these channels. The airline also uses these networks to inform customers of KLM news, marketing campaigns and promotions.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The airline\'s use of social media platforms to reach customers peaked when the Icelandic volcano <a href="/wiki/Eyjafjallaj%C3%B6kull" title="Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull">Eyjafjallaj\xc3\xb6kull</a> erupted in April 2010, causing widespread disruption to air traffic. Customers used the social networks to contact the airline, which used them to provide information about the situation.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Following the increased use of social media, KLM created a centralized, public social media website named the Social Media Hub in October 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM has developed several services based on these social platforms, including:\n</p>\n<ul><li><i>Meet &amp; Seat</i>; this service allows passengers to find information about people who will be on the same KLM flight by connecting their Facebook or LinkedIn profiles to the flight. Meet &amp; Seat facilitates contact with fellow travelers who have the same background or interests.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> By launching Meet &amp; Seat, KLM became the first airline to integrate social networking into its regular flight process.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><i>Trip Planner</i>; this platform uses Facebook to organize a trip with Facebook friends.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Twitterbots; KLM operates several <a href="/wiki/Twitterbot" class="mw-redirect" title="Twitterbot">Twitterbots</a>, including one to request the current status of a flight and one to request the lowest KLM fares to a destination on a specified date or month.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<p>In June 2013, KLM launched its own 3D strategy game "Aviation Empire" for <a href="/wiki/IOS" title="IOS">iOS</a> and <a href="/wiki/Android_(operating_system)" title="Android (operating system)">Android</a> platforms. The game allows users to experience airline management. Players manage KLM from its establishment until the present; they can by investing in a fleet, build a network with international destinations and develop airports. The game combines the digital world with the real world by enabling the unlocking of airports by <a href="/wiki/GPS" class="mw-redirect" title="GPS">GPS</a> check-ins.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Philanthropy">Philanthropy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Philanthropy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM started KLM AirCares, a program that aids underprivileged children in developing countries to which KLM flies, in 1999.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup> The airline collects money and airmiles from passengers. In 2012, new applications for support from the program were suspended because it needed an overhaul.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Destinations">Destinations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Destinations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_KLM_destinations" title="List of KLM destinations">List of KLM destinations</a></div>\n<p>KLM and its partners serve 133 destinations in 70 countries on five continents from their hub at <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Airport_Schiphol" title="Amsterdam Airport Schiphol">Amsterdam Airport Schiphol</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Codeshare agreements bring the total amount of destinations available via KLM to 826.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Codeshare_agreements">Codeshare agreements</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Codeshare agreements">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM has <a href="/wiki/Codeshare_agreement" title="Codeshare agreement">codeshare agreements</a> with the following airlines:<sup id="cite_ref-CAPA_KLM_profile_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CAPA_KLM_profile-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r998391716">.mw-parser-output .div-col{margin-top:0.3em;column-width:30em}.mw-parser-output .div-col-small{font-size:90%}.mw-parser-output .div-col dd{page-break-inside:avoid;break-inside:avoid-column}</style><div class="div-col" style="column-width: 17em;">\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Aer_Lingus" title="Aer Lingus">Aer
