href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/XiamenAir" title="XiamenAir">XiamenAir</a></li></ul>\n</div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet">Fleet</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Fleet">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/KLM_fleet" title="KLM fleet">KLM fleet</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Fleet_strategy">Fleet strategy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Fleet strategy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM\'s first of 8 Boeing 787-10 aircraft was delivered on 28 June 2019; it featured 100th anniversary markings.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>On 19 June 2013, KLM had ordered 7 <a href="/wiki/Airbus_A350_XWB" class="mw-redirect" title="Airbus A350 XWB">Airbus A350-900s</a>. In June 2019, Air France\xe2\x80\x93KLM announced that KLM will not take up any of the group\'s ordered A350s, because of fleet rationalization purposes.\n</p><p>CEO Ben Smith has announced at Air France\'s Investor Day (5 November 2019) in Paris that "in the near future" KLM will only use the 777 and 787 as their long-haul fleet, retiring their 13 A330\'s. This move will make KLM an all-Boeing airline.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Special_liveries">Special liveries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Special liveries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Royal_Dutch_Airlines_Boeing_787-10_Dreamliner_PH-BKA_(100_Years_livery).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_PH-BVA_in_TPE_AUG_2017.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/KLM_PH-BVA_in_TPE_AUG_2017.jpg/220px-KLM_PH-BVA_in_TPE_AUG_2017.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/cb/KLM_PH-BVA_in_TPE_AUG_2017.jpg/330px-KLM_PH-BVA_in_TPE_AUG_2017.jpg 1.5x, livery.</div></div></div>\n<p>KLM has several aircraft painted in special liveries; they include:\n</p>\n<ul><li>PH-BVA, a Boeing 777-300ER, features an orange forward fuselage that fades into the standard blue to commemorate the Netherlands national team\'s participation in the <a href="/wiki/2016_Summer_Olympics" title="2016 Summer Olympics">2016 Summer Olympics</a> in <a href="/wiki/Rio_de_Janeiro" title="Rio de Janeiro">Rio de Janeiro</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>PH-KZU, a Fokker F70, has been applied with a special livery featuring <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Fokker" title="Anthony Fokker">Anthony Fokker</a>, the founder of <a href="/wiki/Fokker" title="Fokker">Fokker</a>, commemorating the airline\'s long-standing history with Fokker aircraft and the phase-out of the <a href="/wiki/Fokker_70" title="Fokker 70">Fokker 70</a> aircraft in October 2017.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></li>\n<li>Several aircraft bear the silver SkyTeam alliance livery, including PH-BVD (a 777-300ER), PH-BXO (a 737-900), and PH-EZX (a KLM Cityhopper ERJ-190).</li>\n<li>PH-BKA, a Boeing 787-10, features the standard KLM livery with a 100 wrapped around its lettering on the plane, this is because of the 100 years of being an established airline.</li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cabin">Cabin</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Cabin">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>KLM has three cabin classes for international long-haul routes; World Business Class, Economy Comfort and Economy. Personal screens with audio-video on-demand, satellite telephone, SMS, and e-mail services are available in all cabins on all long-haul aircraft. European short-haul and medium-haul flights have Economy seats in the rear cabin, and Economy Comfort and Europe Business in the forward cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="World_Business_Class">World Business Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: World Business Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg/220px-KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="214" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg/330px-KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg/440px-KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3018" data-file-height="2937" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_World_Business_Class_Seat.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A Business Class seat on board a former refurbished KLM <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747-400</a>.</div></div></div>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg/220px-KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg/330px-KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg/440px-KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="2448" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_787-9_Economy_class.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Economy Comfort and Economy Class seats on board a KLM <a href="/wiki/Boeing_787" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 787">Boeing 787-9 Dreamliner</a>.</div></div></div>\n<p>World Business Class is KLM\'s long-haul business class product. Seats in the older World Business Class are 20 inches (51&#160;cm) wide and have a 60-inch (150&#160;cm) <a href="/wiki/Seat_pitch" class="mw-redirect" title="Seat pitch">pitch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-seatinformation_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatinformation-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Seats can be reclined into a 170-degree angled flat bed with a length of 75 inches (190&#160;cm). Seats are equipped with a 10.4-inch (26&#160;cm) personal entertainment system with audio and video on demand in the armrest, privacy canopy, massage function and laptop power ports.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> World Business Class seating is in a 2\xe2\x80\x932\xe2\x80\x932 abreast arrangement on all Airbus A330s.\n</p><p>In March 2013, KLM introduced a new World Business Class seat to the long-haul fleet. Dutch designer Hella Jongerius designed the new cabin. The diamond-type seat is manufactured by <a href="/wiki/B/E_Aerospace" title="B/E Aerospace">B/E Aerospace</a> and is currently installed on all Airbus A330s and Boeing 777s. The seats were also refurbished on former KLM Boeing 747-400s between 2013 and 2014. The new seats are fully flat and offer 17-inch (43&#160;cm)-high definition personal entertainment systems. When fully flat, the bed is about 2 metres (6.6&#160;ft) long. The cabin features a <a href="/wiki/Cradle-to-cradle" class="mw-redirect" title="Cradle-to-cradle">cradle-to-cradle</a> carpet made from old uniforms woven in an intricate pattern, which is combined with new pillows and curtains with a similar design.<sup id="cite_ref-WBCOverhaul_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WBCOverhaul-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>A completely new design of Business Class seat was introduced with the launch of KLM\'s Boeing 787; this aircraft\'s business class seats are based on the Zodiac Cirrus platform used by Air France. The new seats lie fully flat, with a 1-2-1 layout so every passenger has direct aisle access, a large side-storage area and 16-inch (41&#160;cm) HD video screen.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup> Dutch design group <a href="/wiki/Viktor_%26_Rolf" title="Viktor &amp; Rolf">Viktor &amp; Rolf</a> has designed and provides amenity kits to World Business Class passengers. A new design will be introduced each year and the color of the kits will change every six months. The kit contains socks, eye mask, toothbrush, toothpaste, earplugs and Viktor &amp; Rolf lip balm.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-OMAAT_744_J_review_140-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-OMAAT_744_J_review-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Europe_Business_Class">Europe Business Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Europe Business Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Europe Business Class is KLM\'s and KLM Cityhopper\'s short-haul business-class. Europe Business Class seats are 17-inch (43&#160;cm) wide and have an average pitch of 33 inches (84&#160;cm).<sup id="cite_ref-seatinformation_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatinformation-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> Middle seats in rows of three are blocked to increase passengers\' personal space. Europe Business Class seats feature extra legroom and recline further than regular Economy Class seats. In-seat power is available on all <a href="/wiki/Boeing_737_Next_Generation" title="Boeing 737 Next Generation">Boeing 737</a> aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup> Europe Business Class has no personal entertainment. Seating is arranged 3\xe2\x80\x933 abreast with the middle seat blocked on the Boeing 737 aircraft, and a 2\xe2\x80\x932 abreast arrangement on the Embraer 190 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-seatingplans_143-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatingplans-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_Comfort">Economy Comfort</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Economy Comfort">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Economy Comfort is the premium economy class offered on all KLM and KLM Cityhopper flights. Economy Comfort seats on long-haul flights have 4 inches (10&#160;cm) more pitch than Economy Class, a 35\xe2\x80\x9336-inch (89\xe2\x80\x9391&#160;cm) pitch and recline up to 7 inches (18&#160;cm); double the recline of Economy.<sup id="cite_ref-economyseatsintercontinental_144-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economyseatsintercontinental-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> Economy Comfort seats on short-haul flights have 3.5 inches (8.9&#160;cm) more pitch, totaling 33.5\xe2\x80\x9334.5-inch (85\xe2\x80\x9388&#160;cm), and can recline up to 5 inches (13&#160;cm) (40%) further.<sup id="cite_ref-economyseatseurope_145-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economyseatseurope-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup> Except for the increased pitch and recline, seating and service in Economy Comfort is the same as in Economy Class. Economy Comfort is located in a separate cabin before the Economy Class; passengers can exit the aircraft before Economy passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-ECComfortAdvantages_146-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECComfortAdvantages-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Economy Comfort seats can be reserved by Economy Class passengers. The service is free for passengers with a full-fare ticket, for Flying Blue Platinum members and Delta Air Lines <a href="/wiki/SkyMiles" title="SkyMiles">SkyMiles</a> Platinum or Diamond members. Discounts apply for Flying Blue Silver or Gold members, SkyTeam Elite Plus members and Delta SkyMiles members.<sup id="cite_ref-ECComfortAdvantages_146-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ECComfortAdvantages-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy_Class">Economy Class</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Economy Class">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>The Economy Class seats on long-haul flights have a 31-to-32-inch (79\xe2\x80\x9381&#160;cm) pitch and are 17.5 inches (44&#160;cm) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-seatinformation_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatinformation-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-economyseatsintercontinental_144-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economyseatsintercontinental-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> All seats are equipped with adjustable winged headrests, a 9-inch (23&#160;cm) PTV with AVOD, and a personal handset satellite telephone that can be used with a credit card. Economy Class seats in Airbus A330-300 aircraft are also equipped with in-seat power.<sup id="cite_ref-seatinformation_133-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatinformation-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> The Economy Class seats on short-haul flights have a 30-to-31-inch (76\xe2\x80\x9379&#160;cm) pitch and are 17 inches (43&#160;cm) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-seatinformation_133-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatinformation-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-economyseatsintercontinental_144-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-economyseatsintercontinental-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> The Economy Class seats on short-haul flights do not feature any personal entertainment. The long-haul Economy Class seating is in a 3\xe2\x80\x934\xe2\x80\x933 abreast arrangement on the Boeing 747-400, Boeing 777-300ER aircraft and on Boeing 777-200ER aircraft, a 3-3-3 abreast arrangement on the Boeing 787-9 aircraft, and a 2\xe2\x80\x934\xe2\x80\x932 abreast arrangement on the Airbus A330 aircraft. The short-haul Economy Class seating is in a 3\xe2\x80\x933 abreast arrangement on the Boeing 737 aircraft and a 2\xe2\x80\x932 abreast arrangement on the Embraer 175 and 190 aircraft, and the seats on these aircraft are 17 inches (43&#160;cm) wide.<sup id="cite_ref-seatingplans_143-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-seatingplans-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Services">Services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<table class="box-Advert plainlinks metadata ambox ambox-content ambox-Advert" role="presentation"><tbody><tr><td class="mbox-image"><div style="width:52px"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/40px-Ambox_important.svg.png" decoding="async" width="40" height="40" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/60px-Ambox_important.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/b/b4/Ambox_important.svg/80px-Ambox_important.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="40" data-file-height="40" /></div></td><td class="mbox-text"><div Wikipedia is not">an advertisement</a></b>.<span class="hide-when-compact"> Please help <a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit">improve it</a> by removing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Spam" title="Wikipedia:Spam">promotional content</a> and inappropriate <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:External_links#Advertising_and_conflicts_of_interest" title="Help:Maintenance template removal">Learn how and when to remove this template message</a>)</i></small></div></td></tr></tbody></table>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="In-flight_entertainment">In-flight entertainment</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: In-flight entertainment">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM\'s <a href="/wiki/In-flight_entertainment" title="In-flight entertainment">in-flight entertainment</a> system is available in all classes on all widebody aircraft; it provides all passengers with <a href="/wiki/Video_on_demand" title="Video on demand">Audio/Video on Demand</a> (AVOD). The system includes interactive entertainment including movies, television programs, music, games, and language courses. About 80 movies including recent releases, classics and world cinema are available in several languages. The selection is changed every month.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup> The in-flight entertainment system can be used to send SMS text messages and emails to the ground. <a href="/wiki/Panasonic" title="Panasonic">Panasonic</a>\'s 3000i system is installed on all Boeing 747-400, Boeing 777-200ER, and on most of the Airbus A330-200 aircraft.<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> All Airbus A330-300 and Boeing 777-300ER aircraft, and some Airbus A330-200 aircraft are fitted with the Panasonic eX2 in-flight entertainment system.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM provides a selection of international newspapers to its passengers on long-haul flights; on short-haul flights they are only offered to Europe Business Class passengers. A selection of international magazines is available for World Business Class passengers on long-haul flights.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> All passengers are provided with KLM\'s in-flight magazine, the <i><a href="/wiki/Holland_Herald" title="Holland Herald">Holland Herald</a>.</i><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> On board flights to China, South Korea and Japan, the airline offers in-flight magazines <i>EuroSky</i> (China and Japan), in either Chinese or Japanese, and <i>Wings of Europe</i> (South Korea) in Korean.<sup id="cite_ref-asiaservices_153-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asiaservices-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> On 29 May 2013, KLM and Air France launched a pilot scheme to test in-flight <a href="/wiki/Wi-Fi" title="Wi-Fi">Wi-Fi</a> internet access. Each airline equipped one Boeing 777-300ER in its fleet with Wi-Fi, which passengers can use with their Wi-Fi-enabled devices. Wireless service was available after the aircraft reached 20,000 feet (6,100&#160;m) in altitude.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Catering">Catering</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Catering">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>World Business Class passengers are served a three-course meal. Each year KLM partners with a leading Dutch chef to develop the dishes that are served on board. Passengers in Europe Business Class are served either a cold meal, a hot main course, or a three-course meal depending on the duration of the flight.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup> All chicken served in World and Europe Business Class meets the standards of the Dutch Beter Leven Keurmerk (Better Life Quality Mark).<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> KLM partnered with Dutch designer <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Wanders" title="Marcel Wanders">Marcel Wanders</a> to design the tableware of World and European Business Class.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Economy Class passengers on long-haul flights are served a hot meal and a snack, and second hot meal or breakfast, depending on the duration of the flight. On short-haul flights, passengers are served sandwiches or a choice of sweet or savoury snack, depending on the duration and time of the day. If the flight is at least two hours long, "stroopwafel" cookies are served before the descent. Most alcoholic beverages are free-of-charge for all passengers. After a successful trial period, KLM introduced \xc3\xa0 la carte meals in Economy Class on 14 September 2011; Dutch, Japanese, Italian, cold delicacies, and Indonesian meals are offered.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Special meals, include children\'s, vegetarian, medical, and religious meals, can be requested in each class up to 24 or 36 hours before departure.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> On flights to India, China, South Korea, and Japan, KLM offers authentic Asian meals in all classes.<sup id="cite_ref-asiaservices_153-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-asiaservices-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup> Meals served on KLM flights departing from Amsterdam are provided by KLM Catering Services.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In September 2016, KLM launched the world\'s first in-flight draft beer under the partnership with <a href="/wiki/Heineken" title="Heineken">Heineken</a>. The new service made its premiere aboard a flight to <a href="/wiki/Cura%C3%A7ao" title="Cura\xc3\xa7ao">Cura\xc3\xa7ao</a> in the airline\'s World Business Class cabin.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Delft_Blue_houses">Delft Blue houses</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Delft Blue houses">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_KLM_Delft_Blue_houses" title="List of KLM Delft Blue houses">List of KLM Delft Blue houses</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG/220px-KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG" decoding="async" width="220" height="105" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG/330px-KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2c/KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG/440px-KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG 2x" data-file-width="595" data-file-height="283" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_DelftBlueHouses.PNG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>KLM Delft Blue Houses.</div></div></div>\n<p>Since the 1950s, KLM has presented its World Business Class passengers with a <a href="/wiki/Delft_blue" class="mw-redirect" title="Delft blue">Delft blue</a> miniature traditional Dutch house.<sup id="cite_ref-kingdom_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingdom-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup> These miniatures are reproductions of real Dutch houses and are filled with Dutch <a href="/wiki/Genever" class="mw-redirect" title="Genever">genever</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHouses_164-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHouses-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> Initially the houses were filled with <a href="/wiki/Bols_(brand)" title="Bols (brand)">Bols</a> liqueur, which in 1986 was changed to Bols young genever.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>In 1952, KLM started to give the houses to its First Class passengers. With the elimination of First Class in 1993, the houses were handed out to all Business Class passengers.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJHouses_166-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJHouses-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> The impetus for these houses was a rule aimed at curtailing a previously widespread practise of offering incentives to passengers by limiting the value of gifts given by airlines to $0.75 USD. KLM did not bill the Delft Blue houses as a gift, but as a last drink on the house, which was served in the house.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJHouses_166-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJHouses-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Every year, a new house is presented on 7 October, the anniversary of KLM\'s founding in 1919.<sup id="cite_ref-KLMHouses_164-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-KLMHouses-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup> The number on the last-presented house thus represents the number of years KLM has been in operation. Special edition houses\xe2\x80\x94the <a href="/wiki/Dutch_Royal_Palace" class="mw-redirect" title="Dutch Royal Palace">Dutch Royal Palace</a> and the 17th century Cheese Weighing House <i>De Waag</i> in <a href="/wiki/Gouda,_South_Holland" title="Gouda, South Holland">Gouda</a>\xe2\x80\x94are offered to special guests, such as VIPs and honeymoon couples.<sup id="cite_ref-WSJHouses_166-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-WSJHouses-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ground_services">Ground services</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Ground services">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM offers various check-in methods to its passengers, who can check in for their flights at self-service check-in kiosks at the airport, via the Internet, or a mobile telephone or tablet. At destinations where these facilities are not available, check-in is by an airline representative at the counter. Electronic boarding passes can be received on a mobile device while boarding passes can be printed at airport kiosks.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Since 4 July 2008 KLM, in cooperation with Amsterdam Airport Schiphol, has been offering self-service baggage drop-off to its passengers. The project started with a trial that included one drop-off point.<sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The number of these points has gradually increased; as of 8&#160;February&#160;2012<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> there are 12 of them.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup> KLM passengers can now drop off their bags themselves. Before they are allowed to do that they are being checked by a KLM employee.\n</p><p>In November 2012, KLM started a pilot scheme at Amsterdam Airport Schiphol to test self-service boarding. Passengers boarded the aircraft without any interference of a gate agent by scanning their <a href="/wiki/Boarding_pass" title="Boarding pass">boarding passes</a>, which opened a gate. KLM partner airline Air France ran the same pilot at its hub at <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport">Paris-Charles de Gaulle Airport</a>. The pilot ran until March 2013, which was followed by an evaluation.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM is the first airline to offer self-service transfer kiosks on its European and intercontinental routes for passengers connecting through Amsterdam Airport Schiphol.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup> The kiosks enable connecting passengers to view flight details of connecting flights, to change seat assignments or upgrade to a more comfortable seat. When a passenger misses a connecting flight, details about alternative flights can be viewed on the kiosk and a new boarding pass can be printed. Passengers who are entitled to coupons for a beverage, meal, the use of a telephone, or a travel discount can have these printed at the kiosk.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Bus_services_and_train_codeshares">Bus services and train codeshares</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Bus services and train codeshares">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>KLM has bus services for customers living in certain cities without flights from KLM, transporting them to airports where they may board KLM flights. It operates buses from <a href="/wiki/Nijmegen_railway_station" title="Nijmegen railway station">Nijmegen railway station</a> and <a href="/wiki/Arnhem_Central_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Arnhem Central Station">Arnhem Central Station</a> in the Netherlands to Amsterdam Schiphol, from <a href="/wiki/Maastricht_railway_station" title="Maastricht railway station">Maastricht railway station</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>-code ZYT) via <a href="/wiki/Maastricht-Aachen_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Maastricht-Aachen Airport">Maastricht-Aachen Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>-code MST) and <a href="/wiki/Eindhoven_Airport" title="Eindhoven Airport">Eindhoven Airport</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>-code EIN) to <a href="/wiki/Amsterdam_Schiphol" class="mw-redirect" title="Amsterdam Schiphol">Amsterdam Schiphol</a> (<a href="/wiki/IATA" class="mw-redirect" title="IATA">IATA</a>-code AMS), and from <a href="/wiki/Ottawa_Railway_Station" class="mw-redirect" title="Ottawa Railway Station">Ottawa Railway Station</a> to <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Dorval_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal Dorval Airport">Montreal Dorval Airport</a> in Canada. In addition KLM has codeshares with <a href="/wiki/Thalys" title="Thalys">Thalys</a> and <a href="/wiki/SNCF" title="SNCF">SNCF</a> services so passengers from various French cities may travel to <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle_Airport" title="Charles de Gaulle Airport">Charles de Gaulle Airport</a> and passengers from Belgium may go to Schiphol (from Antwerp) or Charles de Gaulle (from Brussels).<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Flying_Blue">Flying Blue</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: Flying Blue">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Air France-KLM\'s <a href="/wiki/Frequent_flyer_program" class="mw-redirect" title="Frequent flyer program">frequent flyer program</a>, Flying Blue, awards miles based on the distance traveled, ticket fare and class of service. Other airlines that adopted the Flying Blue programme include <a href="/wiki/Air_Europa" title="Air Europa">Air Europa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Garuda_Indonesia" title="Garuda Indonesia">Garuda Indonesia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kenya_Airways" title="Kenya Airways">Kenya Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Aircalin" title="Aircalin">Aircalin</a>, and <a href="/wiki/TAROM" title="TAROM">TAROM</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> Miles can also be earned from all other SkyTeam partners.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup> Membership in the program is free.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Two types of miles can be earned within the Flying Blue program; Award Miles and Level Miles. Award Miles can be exchanged for rewards and expire after 20 months without flying. Level Miles are used to determine membership level and remain valid until 31 December of each year.<sup id="cite_ref-earnmiles_179-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earnmiles-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Award Miles can be earned on Flying Blue partner airlines including <a href="/wiki/Air_Corsica" title="Air Corsica">Air Corsica</a>, <a href="/wiki/Airlinair" title="Airlinair">Airlinair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bangkok_Airways" title="Bangkok Airways">Bangkok Airways</a>, <a href="/wiki/Chalair_Aviation" title="Chalair Aviation">Chalair Aviation</a>, <a href="/wiki/Comair_Limited" class="mw-redirect" title="Comair Limited">Comair</a>, <a href="/wiki/Copa_Airlines" title="Copa Airlines">Copa Airlines</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gol_Transportes_A%C3%A9reos" class="mw-redirect" title="Gol Transportes A\xc3\xa9reos">Gol Transportes A\xc3\xa9reos</a>, Japan Airlines, <a href="/wiki/Malaysia_Airlines" title="Malaysia Airlines">Malaysia Airlines</a>, Qantas, <a href="/wiki/TAAG_Angola" class="mw-redirect" title="TAAG Angola">TAAG Angola</a>, <a href="/wiki/Twin_Jet" title="Twin Jet">Twin Jet</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ukraine_International_Airlines" title="Ukraine International Airlines">Ukraine International Airlines</a>, as well as SkyTeam partners.<sup id="cite_ref-hollandheraldpartners_180-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hollandheraldpartners-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-181" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> Award Miles are redeemable for free tickets, upgrades to a more expensive seating class, extra baggage allowance, and lounge access. They can also be donated to charity through KLM AirCares,<sup id="cite_ref-182" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup> or can be spent in the Flying Blue Store.<sup id="cite_ref-183" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>The Flying Blue programme is divided into four tiers; Explorer, Silver (SkyTeam Elite), Gold (SkyTeam Elite Plus) and Platinum (SkyTeam Elite Plus). Then, you have the special tiers, such as Platinum For Life, ultimate platinum, ultimate platinum skipper, club2000 skipper (for those who did something special for KLM, cannot be requested but will be distributed by KLM).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> The membership tier depends on the number of Level Miles earned and is recalculated each calendar year. Flying Blue privileges are additive by membership tier; higher tiers include all benefits listed for prior tiers. There is an additional fifth tier, Platinum for Life, which can be obtained after 10 consecutive years of Platinum membership. After the Platinum for Life status is obtained, re-qualification is not required.<sup id="cite_ref-platinummember_185-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platinummember-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup> Level Miles can be earned with Air France, KLM, Air Europa, Kenya Airways, TAROM, and other SkyTeam partners.<sup id="cite_ref-earnmiles_179-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-earnmiles-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> Qualification levels and general benefits with SkyTeam airline partners of the Flying Blue tiers are:<sup id="cite_ref-platinummember_185-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-platinummember-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p><b>Flight Bundle</b><sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>KLM offers customers a prepaid flight subscription program called Flight Bundle, which it operates in conjunction with USA based Optiontown Inc.<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>With KLM Flight Bundle, passengers can select one or more destinations in advance for a pre-set, fixed price and decide their travel dates later.&#160; Passengers can customize their own Flight Bundle and depending on the choices they make, can determine the ultimate price for the tickets in the Flight Bundle. Flight Bundle can be shared with family, friends or colleagues.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Incidents_and_accidents">Incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tenerife_airport_disaster">Tenerife airport disaster</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: Tenerife airport disaster">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_(7491686916).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg/220px-KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg/330px-KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg/440px-KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_%287491686916%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3328" data-file-height="1872" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:KLM_Boeing_747-200_PH-BUF_(7491686916).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>At the time of the accident, the <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747" title="Boeing 747">Boeing 747</a> named <i>Rhine</i> was only six years old.</div></div></div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Tenerife_airport_disaster" title="Tenerife airport disaster">Tenerife disaster</a>, which occurred on 27 March 1977, remains the accident with the highest number of airliner passenger fatalities, as well as the most recent fatal and notable incident involving a KLM aircraft. 583 people died when a KLM <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-200B" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-200B">Boeing 747-200B</a> attempted to take off without clearance, and collided with a taxiing <a href="/wiki/Pan_American_World_Airways" class="mw-redirect" title="Pan American World Airways">Pan Am</a> <a href="/wiki/Boeing_747-100" class="mw-redirect" title="Boeing 747-100">Boeing 747-100</a> at <a href="/wiki/Los_Rodeos_Airport" class="mw-redirect" title="Los Rodeos Airport">Los Rodeos Airport</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Canary_Island" class="mw-redirect" title="Canary Island">Canary Island</a> of <a href="/wiki/Tenerife" title="Tenerife">Tenerife</a>, <a href="/wiki/Spain" title="Spain">Spain</a>.  No one on the KLM 747 survived (14 crew, 234 passengers were killed) while 61 of the 396 passengers and crew on the Pan Am aircraft survived. Pilot error from the KLM aircraft was the primary cause. Owing to a communication misunderstanding, the KLM captain thought he had clearance for takeoff.<sup id="cite_ref-Tonyleather_193-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Tonyleather-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> Another cause was dense fog, meaning the KLM flight crew was unable to see the Pan Am aircraft on the runway until immediately prior to the collision.<sup id="cite_ref-ASN_195-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ASN-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> The accident had a lasting influence on the industry, particularly in the area of communication. An increased emphasis was placed on using standardized phraseology in air traffic control (ATC) communication by both controllers and pilots alike, thereby reducing the chance for misunderstandings. As part of these changes, the word "takeoff" was removed from general usage, and is only spoken by ATC when clearing an aircraft to take off.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_incidents_and_accidents">Other incidents and accidents</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: Other incidents and accidents">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_KLM_accidents_and_incidents" title="List of KLM accidents and incidents">List of KLM accidents and incidents</a></div>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_employees">Notable employees</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=KLM&amp;action=edit&amp;section=43" title="Edit section: Notable employees">edit</a><span id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span
